[Brahman.тАФ─Бdhy─Бtmam; rohit─Бdityadevatyam (3. m─Бrut─л; 28-31. ─Бgneyyaс╕е; 31. bahudevaty─Б). tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham: 3-5, 9, 12, 15. jagat─л (15. atij─Бgatagarbh─Б); 8. bhurij; [16.?;] 17. 5-p. kakummat─л jagat─л; 13. ati┼Ы─Бkvaragarbh─Б тАЩtijagat─л*; 14. 3-p. puraс╕еpara┼Ы─Бkvar─Б vipar─лtap─Бdalahс╣гmy─Б pan╠Дkti; 18, 19. 5-p. kakummaty atijagat─л (18. para┼Ы─Бkvar─Б bhurij; 19. par─Бtij─Бgat─Б); 21. ─Бrс╣г─л nicс╣Ыd g─Бyatr─л; 22, 23, 27. pr─Бkс╣Ыt─Б; 26. vir─Бс╣н paroс╣гс╣Зih; 28-30 (28. bhurij), 32, 39, 40, 45-30 and 51-51 [and 57-58]. anuс╣гс╣нubh (52, 55. pathy─Бpan╠Дkti; 55. kakummat─л bс╣Ыhat─лgarbh─Б; 57. katummat─л)тАа; 31. 5-p. kakummat─л ┼Ы─Бkvaragarbh─Б jagat─л; 35. upariс╣гс╣н─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л; 36. nicс╣Ыn mah─Бbс╣Ыhat─л; 37. para┼Ы─Бkvar─Б vir─Бс╕Н atijagat─л; 42. vir─Бс╕Н jagat─л; 43. vir─Бс╣З mah─Бbс╣Ыhat─л; 44. paroс╣гс╣Зih; 59, 60. g─Бyatr─л.]

Comment

Found also in P─Бipp. xviii. тМКwith vs. 30 after 31; vss. 56-57, 59-60 are lacking; vs. 58 is lacking in P─Бipp. xviii., but is found in P─Бipp. xx.тМЛ. A number of the verses are used in various parts of K─Бu┼Ы., and several (four) in V─Бit. *тМКSo the Berlin ms. (against jagat─л of the London ms.): and atijagat─л more nearly fits the vs.тМЛ тАатМКHere the Anukr. text looks as if in disorder: it seems as if yaс╣Б v─Бta (vs. 51) iti с╣гaс╕Н anuс╣гс╣нubhaс╕е ought to refer to the 6 vss. 51, 53-54, 56-58.тМЛ

Translations

Translated: Muir, v. 395 (parts); Ludwig, p. 536; Scherman, p. 73 (parts); Henry, 1, 21; Deussen, Geschichte, i. 1. 218 (cf. his introduction, p. 212 ff.); Griffith, ii. 133; Bloomfield, 207, 661.тАФFurthermore, Bloomfield, in his review (AJP. xii. 429-443) of Henry, discusses a considerable number of passages from this hymn. These discussions will be briefly cited by reference to “AJP. xii.” He considers that the hymn is secondarily “an allegorical exaltation of a king and his queen.”

Translation
  1. Rise up, O powerful one (? v─Бj├нn) that [art] within the waters,
    enter into this kingdom [that is] full of pleasantness; the ruddy one
    (r├│hita) that generated this allтАФlet him bear thee, well-borne, unto
    kingdom.
Notes

R├│hita is evidently a name or form of the sun; and the v─Бjin (Henry,
‘conqueror of booty’) addressed is also the sun. The verse тМКwith faulty
accentsтМЛ is found also in TB. (ii. 5. 2┬╣), which reads тМКasi after y├│
in aтМЛ, ─Б╠Б vi┼Ыa in b, and, for d, s├б no r─Бс╣гс╣нr├йс╣гu s├║dhit─Бс╣Б
dadh─Бtu, which seems better, as removing the difficulty of the sun
establishing the sun. Ppp. reads vi┼Ыvabhс╣Ыtaс╣Б for vi┼Ыvam idam in
c; and it has pipartu for bibhartu at the end; тМКwe had the
converse at xi. 5. 4тМЛ. The resolution ud-─Б╠Б-ihi is required to fill out
the meter of a. All the four hymns of the book (under the name
rohit─Бs) are prescribed in K─Бu┼Ы. 99. 4 to be used in case of a
darkening (eclipse) of the sun. The first half-verse is, according to
K─Бu┼Ы. 49. 18, to be used in the witchcraft ceremony of the
‘water-thunderbolts’ (see x. 5) ‘when the boat sinks.’ тМКCf. AJP. xii.
431.тМЛ

Griffith

Rise, Mighty One, who liest in the waters, and enter this thy fair and glorious kingdom. Let Rohita who made this All uphold thee carefully nurtured for supreme dominion.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Up hath arisen the power (? v─Б╠Бja) that is within the waters; mount
    (─Б-ruh) thou the clans (v├н┼Ы) that are sprung from thee (tv├бdyoni);
    assuming (dh─Б) the soma, the waters, the herbs, the kine, make thou
    the four-footed, the two-footed ones to enter here.
Notes

In b begins the play of words upon the root ruh ‘ascend, mount,
grow,’ and its compounds and derivatives; this play is suggested by the
at least apparent relationship between ruh and rohita, тМКand is found
with considerable elaboration throughoutтМЛ these hymns. Here it doubtless
signifies ‘have supremacy over.’ Ppp. combines in b vi┼Ы─Б тАЭroha, in
c dadh─Бna тАЩpo тАЩс╣гadh-, and in d dvipad─Б тАЩve┼Ы-; and this last
we have to accept in order to make a triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda. In a the
resolution of ─Б╠Б agan, and in b that of tu├бd-, make the meter
right. The Anukr. takes no notice of any irregularity in the verse.

Griffith

The strength that was in waters hath ascended. Mount o’er the tribes which thou hast generated. Creating Soma, waters, plants and cattle, bring hitherward both quadrupeds and bipeds.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Do ye [who are] formidable, O Maruts, sons of the spotted mother,
    with Indra as ally, slaughter our foes; the ruddy one shall listen to
    you, ye liberal ones (sud─Б╠Бnu), ye thrice seven Maruts that enjoy
    sweets together.
Notes

The first half-verse occurred above as v. 21. 11 a, b. We can hardly
help emending triс╣гapt─Б╠Бso to tr├нс╣гapt─Бso. Ppp. reads instead
triс╣гapt─Б. The verse is found also in TB. (ii. 5. 2┬│), which reads in
a ugr─Б (which is better), in b say├║j─Б pr├б с╣З─л╠Бtha (corrupt),
in c a┼Ыс╣Ыс╣Зod abhidyavaс╕е, and in d (with the desired accent)
tr├нsapt─Бso. The verse lacks a syllable (in b) of being a proper
jagat─л.

Griffith

Ye Maruts, strong and mighty, sons of Prisni, with Indra for ally crush down our foemen. Let Rohita, ye bounteous givers, hear you, thrice-seven Maruts who delight in sweetness!

Whitney
Translation
  1. The ruddy one ascended (ruh), mounted the ascents (r├║h); [he,]
    the embryo of the wives, [mounted] the lap of births; him, taken hold
    of by them (f.), the six wide [spaces] discovered; seeing in advance
    the track, he hath brought (─Б-hс╣Ы) hither the kingdom.
Notes

The verse is found also in TB. (ii. 5. 2┬╣), which reads in a (much
better) r├│haс╣Б-rohaс╣Б (for r├║ho ruroha), at the beginning of b
praj─Б╠Бbhir vс╣Ы╠Бddhim, and in c s├бс╣Бrabdho avidat. Such variations
are of interest especially as showing how little connected sense was
recognized in these verses by those who established the texts. This
verse has no right to the name of jagat─л, since all its p─Бdas have a
trochaic close; the two redundant syllables in a and c are
removed by the TB. readings. тМКFor ─Б╠Бh─Бс╕е, see Pr─Бt. ii. 46.тМЛ тМКWith
regard to the transition-sound between -dan and с╣г├бс╕Н, see Pr─Бt. ii.
9, note.тМЛ

Griffith

Up to the lap of births, to lofty places, hath Rohita, the germ of Dames, ascended. Conjoined with these he found the six realms: seeing his way in front here he received the kingship.

    scattered; fearlessness hath become thine; unto thee, being such, let

    ┼Ы├бkvar─лs.

Griffith

For thee hath Rohita obtained dominion, scattered thine ene- mies, become thy safeguard. So by the potent Sakvaris let Heaven and Earth be milked to- yield thee all thy wishes.

Translation
  1. The ruddy one generated heaven-and-earth; there the most exalted one
    stretched the line (t├бntu); there was supported (┼Ыri) the one-footed
    goat (? aj├б); by strength he made firm (dс╣Ыh) heaven-and-earth.
Notes

Ppp. reads in c ekap─Бd yo. The verse occurs in TB. (ii. 5. 2┬│),
with only slight variants: t├бsmin for t├бtra in b and c, and
├йkap─Бt in c. тМКC┬г. AJP. xii. 443.тМЛ

Griffith

Rohita gave the Earth and Heavens their being. There Para- meshthin held the cord extended. Thereon reposeth Aja Ekapada. He with his might hath stab- lished Earth and Heaven.

Translation
  1. The ruddy one made firm heaven-and-earth; by him was established the
    sky (sv├аr), by him the firmament (n─Б╠Бka); by him the atmosphere, the
    spaces (r├бjas) were measured out; by him the gods discovered
    immortality (amс╣Ы╠Бta).

differently: s├│ ant├бrikс╣гe r├бjaso vim─Б╠Бnas t├йna dev─Б╠Бс╕е s├║var ├бnv avindan.

Griffith

Rohita firmly stablished Earth and Heaven: by him was ether fixt by him the welkin. He measured out mid air and all the regions: by him the Gods found life that lasts for ever.

  1. The ruddy one examined (vi-mс╣Ы┼Ы) the all-formed, collecting to

    ghee.

Griffith

Arranging shoots, springs, Rohita considered this Universe in all its forms and phases. May he, gone up to heaven with mighty glory, anoint thy sov- ranty with milk and fatness.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What ascents, fore-ascents thou hast, what on-ascents (─Бr├║h) thou
    hast, with which thou fillest the sky, the atmosphere, with the
    br├бhman, with the milk of them increasing, do thou watch over the
    people (v├н┼Ы) in the kingdom of the ruddy one.
Notes

Though the first three p─Бdas count 12 syllables each, only a is
jagat─л in structure. With a, b compare xviii. 2. 9 a, b. тМКFor
vss. 8-9, see AJP. xii. 433.тМЛ

Griffith

Thy risings up, thy mountings and ascensions wherewith thou fillest heaven and air’s mid-region– By prayer for these, by milk of these, increasing, in Rohita’s kingdom watch, among his people.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What clans (v├н┼Ы) of thine came into being out of ardor (t├бpas),
    those have come hither after the young (vats├б), the g─Бyatr─л╠Б; let
    them enter (─Б-vi┼Ы) into thee with propitious mind; let the ruddy young
    with its mother go against [them].
Notes

Or (in a) ‘what clans came into being out of thy heat.’ In b,
the pada-text has ih├б: ─Б╠Б: aguс╕е. In d, s├бmm─Бt─Б means more
probably ‘having a common mother,’ but the sense is too obscure to allow
of much confidence in any translation. The TB. version (ii. 5. 2┬▓) reads
in a t├бpas─Б (better); for b, g─Бyatr├бс╣Б vats├бm ├бnu t─Б╠Бs ta ─Б╠Б
тАЩguс╕е; in c, m├бhas─Б sv├йna; in d, putr├│ (for vats├│). The
Anukr. does not heed that the last p─Бda is jagat─л. Ppp. combines in
d vatso тАШbhy.

Griffith

The tribes thy heat produced have followed hither the Calf and Gayatri, the strain that lauds him. With friendly heart let them approach to serve thee, and the Calf Rohita come with his mother.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The ruddy one hath stood aloft upon the firmament (n─Б╠Бk─Б),
    generating all forms, [he,] young, poet; Agni shineth forth with keen
    light; in the third space (r├бjas) he hath done dear things.
Notes

Ppp. reads bh─Бsi in c. The Anukr. again passes without notice the
jagat─л p─Бda b. тМКW. suggests by interlineation as alternative,
‘hath made for himself dear forms.’тМЛ

Griffith

Erected, Rohita hath reached the welkin, wise, young, creating every form and figure. Agni, refulgent with his heightened lustre, in the third realm hath brought us joy and gladness.

Griffith

Thousand-horned Bull, may Jatavedas, worshipped with butter, balmed with Soma, rich in heroes, Besought, ne’er quit me; may I ne’er forsake thee. Give me abundant men and herds of cattle.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The ruddy one is generator and mouth of the sacrifice; to the ruddy
    one I make oblation with speech, with hearing, with mind; to the ruddy
    one go the gods with favoring mind; let him cause me to ascend with
    ascensions (r├│ha) of meeting (s─Бmity├б).
Notes

The pada-texts read blunderingly in d s─Бmре░aity─Б├н (instead of
-y─Б├нс╕е). Henry emends to samity─Б├н ‘in order to union with him’; but
s├бmiti has the well-established sense of ‘meeting, gathering,
assembly’; hence Ludwig (for roh─Бiс╕е s-) ‘with abundant success in the
samiti.’ тМКSee AJP. xii. 434.тМЛ Ppp. reads at the end rohay─Бti. The
verse is kindred with ii. 35. 5 in general expression. Its metrical
structure (12 + 15: 13 + 11 = 51) is wholly irregular; the definition of
the Anukr. тМК52 syllablesтМЛ тМКnearlyтМЛ fits it mechanically.

Griffith

Rohita is the sire and mouth of worship: to him with voice, ear, heart I pay oblation. To Rohita come Gods with joyful spirit. May he by risings raise me till I join him.

Notes

dadh─Бt. The metrical definition implies the resolution v├н ad-, and
two resolutions in b (-si ├║pa and m─Б im-, doubtless), to make a
pan╠Дkti (14 + 12: 14 = 40).

Griffith

Rohita ordered sacrifice for Visvakarman: thence have I obta- ined this strength and energy. May I proclaim thee as my kin over the greatness of the world.

резрем рдЕрдпрдВ рд╡рд╕реНрддреЗ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. This one clothes himself in the embryo (womb?) of the earth; this
    one clothes himself in the sky, the atmosphere; this one, on the summit
    of the reddish one, has penetrated the heaven (sv├аr), the worlds.
Notes

Ppp. reads viс╣гс╣нapas sv- in c-d, and sam ─Бna┼Ыe in d. The
verse (9 + 9: 8 + 8 = 34) seems to be overlooked in the Anukr., or its
definition has dropped out of the mss. Verses 16-20 are prescribed in
K─Бu┼Ы. 54. 10 to accompany, in the god─Бna-ceremony, the dressing of the
child in a new garment. They are much better suited to that use than to
their surroundings here.

Griffith

He goes into the womb of earth, he robes himself in heaven and air. He on the Bright One’s station hath reached heavenly light and all the worlds.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O lord of speech, [be] earth pleasant to us; [be] the lair
    (y├│ni) pleasant, [be] our couch very propitious; just here be breath
    in our companionship; thee here, O most exalted one, let Agni surround
    with life-time, with honor.
Notes

Henry understands sakhy├й as dat. of s├бkhi, against the accent. The
Anukr. apparently views the verse as тМК10 + 10: 10 + 12 + 6 = 48тМЛ. The
verse (with the two following?) is included among the v─Бcaspatilin╠Дg─Бs,
used in K─Бu┼Ы. 41. 15 in a ceremony for good luck. Ppp. reads at the end
-с╣гс╣нhi pary ahaс╣Б varcas─Б dadh─Бmi.

Griffith

To us, Vachaspati, may Earth be pleasant, pleasant our dwelling, pleasant be our couches. Even here may Prana be our friend: may Agni, O Parameshthin give thee life and splendour.

    into being as Vi┼Ыvakarman’sтАФjust here be breath in our companionship;

    life-time, with honor.

Translation
  1. O lord of speech, [generate] well-willing and mind; generate kine
    in our stall (goс╣гс╣нh├б), progeny in our wombs (y├│ni); just here be

    with life-time, with honor.

omitting, as before, ─Бyuс╣г─Б, тМКand having again dadh─Бtu at the end,

Griffith

Breed, O Vachaspati, joy and understanding, kine i n our stall and children in our consorts. Even here may Prana be our friend: may Agni, O Parameshthin, give thee life and splendour.

Whitney
Translation
  1. May Savitar, god Agni, surround thee [with honor]; with honor may
    Mitra-and-Varuс╣Зa deck (abhiтМК+dh─БтМЛ) thee; striding down all niggards
    come thou; thou hast made this kingdom full of pleasantness.
Notes

The shift from p├бri in a to abh├н in b makes a mixed and
difficult construction. Ppp. combines devo тАШgnir in a and sarv─Б
тАЩr─Бt─лr in c, and reads (better) kс╣Ыс╣Зuhi in d.

Griffith

With splendour let God Savitar, and Agni, with splendour Mitra, Varuna invest thee. Treading down all Malignities, come hither. Pleasant and’ glorious hast thou made this kingdom.

Translation
  1. Thou whom the spotted one (f.), the side-horse, draws (vah) in the
    chariot, O ruddy one, thou goest with brightness (┼Ы├║bh), making flow
    the waters.
Notes

This verse corresponds to RV. viii. 7. 28, which, however, has
considerable variants: for a, y├бd eс╣г─Бm pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гat─л (p. -t─лс╕е) r├бthe;
in b, r├│hitaс╕е; in c, y─Б╠Бnti ┼Ыubhr─Б╠Б (p. -r─Б╠Бс╕е). As is usual
in such cases, some of our mss. read pс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣нis in b, and с╣Ыс╣З├бn in
c. And most read rohitaс╕е тМКunaccentedтМЛ at end of b (only
Bs.R.K. -ta), as if under influence of the RV. version. тМКSPP. adopts
in his text rohita, but reports six of his mss. as giving rohitaс╕е,
without accent.тМЛ Ppp. adds at the end tene тАЩmaс╣Б brahmaс╣Зaspate ruhaс╣Б
rohayo тАЩttamam. The verse is quoted in a ceremony for prosperity’ by
K─Бu┼Ы. (24. 42), which volunteers the added explanation dy─Бuс╕е pс╣Ыс╣гaty
─Бdityo rohitaс╕е; and it is also included among the puс╣гс╣нika mantras:
see note to K─Бu┼Ы. 19. 1. K─Бu┼Ы. 24. 43 states further that a spotted cow
is given (as sacrificial fee); and the comm. appears to direct that vss.
21-26 accompany the gift.

Rohita, car-borne by a speckled leader, thou, pouring water,. goest on in triumph.

-p─Бс╣Е ja- тМКPr─Бt. ii. 11тМЛ. M.p.m. тМКand SPP’s C.тМЛ read at end sy─Бma;

Golden, refulgent, lofty is the Lady, Rohini, Rohita’s devoted Consort. Through her may we win various spoil and booty, through her be conquerors in every battle.

Translation
  1. Here the seat (s├бdas), she that is ruddy, of the ruddy one; yonder
    the road by which the spotted one (f.) goes; her the Gandharvas, the

Notes

All the mss. except O.D. (and these differ perhaps only by accident)

Griffith

Rohita’s seat is Rohini before us: that is the path the speckled Mare pursueth. Kasyapas and Gandharvas lead her upward, and heavenly sages ever watch and guard her,

Whitney
Translation
  1. The ruddy one, the sharp-horned bull, who encompassed Agni, the sun,
    who props asunder (vi-stabh) the earth and the heavenтАФout of him do
    the gods create creations.
Notes

Ppp. begins with ayaс╣Б roh-. The curious reading of O. in c,
с╣гс╣нab-h-n─Бti (the b and h two different letters), was noted above,
under xii. 4. 4. тМК“Encompassed”: Bloomfield, “became superior to,” AJP.
xii. 443.тМЛ K─Бu┼Ы. 18. 25 gives the verse, in company with several others,
as to be used in the so-called citr─Бkarman (ceremony concerning the
asterism citr─Б) to accompany the partaking of a milk rice-dish; and
the Paddhati includes both it and the following verse in the salila
gaс╣Зa.

Griffith

Rohita, Bull whose horns are sharply pointed, superior of Agni and of Surya, He who supports the sundered earth and heaven,–from him the Gods effect their own creations.

  1. Agni, kindled, being kindled, increased with ghee, offered to with
    gheeтАФlet the overpowering, all-overpowering Agni slay them who are my
    rivals.

accompany the laying of bonds upon the “boat” there treated of; тМКrather,

Griffith

Both kindling and inflamed, adored with butter and enhanced thereby. May conquering Agni, conqueror of all, destroy mine enemies.

Whitney
Translation
  1. O Agni, make our rivals fall below us; stagger the truculent
    (utp├нp─Бna) fellow, O Brihaspati; O Indra-and-Agni, O Mitra-and-Varuс╣Зa,
    let them fall below [us], impotent in their fury.
Notes

Lit. ’not making their fury effective against’ us. The Anukr. apparently
understands the structure of the verse as 12 + 14: 8 + 6 + 8 = 48; but
there is no good reason for dividing the last redundant p─Бda into two.
Ppp. reads utapid─Бnaс╣Б (for utpip─Бnam тМКdiscussed AJP. xii. 441тМЛ) in
b.

Griffith

Cast down our foes beneath our feet, O Agni. Brihaspati, oppress our rebel kinsman. Low let them fall, O Indra-Agni. Mitra-Varuna, powerless to show their anger.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The young (vats├б) of the vir─Б╠Бj, the bull of prayers (mat├н),
    mounted, bright-backed, the atmosphere; with ghee they sing (arc) the
    song (ark├б) unto the young; him, being br├бhman, they increase with
    br├бhman.
Notes

Ppp. combines in b -pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нho ant-. TB. (ii. 8. 8тБ╣) has a
corresponding verse, but with numerous variants: pit─Б╠Б vir─Б╠Бj─Бm с╣Ыс╣гabh├│
ray─лс╣З─Б╠Бm ant├бrikс╣гaс╣Б vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpa ─Б╠Б vive┼Ыa: t├бm ark─Б├нr abhy ├аrcanti vats├бm
br├бhma s├бntam br├бhmaс╣З─Б vardh├бyantaс╕е. тМКBloomfield, AJP. xii. 441, would
emend ark├бm to akt├бm; but the TB. variant is very much against it.тМЛ
Our verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 12. 4, at the end of a charm for securing
one’s wishes.

Griffith

Calf of Viraj, the Bull of prayers and worship, whitebacked, he hath gone up to air’s mid-region. Singing, they hymn the Calf, with gifts of butter: him who is Brahma they exalt with Brahma.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Both ascend thou to heaven and ascend to earth; both ascend to
    kingdom and ascend to property; both ascend to progeny and ascend to
    immortality; make thyself contiguous with the ruddy one.
Notes

The verse is quoted in V─Бit. 13. 5 to accompany the leading up of the
cow that is to be exchanged for the soma-plant.

Griffith

Rise up to earth, rise up to heaven above it; rise up to opulence, rise up to kingship. Rise up to offspring, rise to life immortal; rise, and with Rohita unite thy body.

Griffith

With all the Gods who circle round the Sun, upholding royal sway, With all of these may Rohita accordant, give sovranty to thee with friendly spirit.

Griffith

Cleansed by prayer, sacrifices bear thee upward: bay coursers, ever travelling, convey thee. Thy light shines over sea and billowy ocean.

Translation
  1. On the ruddy one are set (┼Ыrit├б) heaven-and-earth, on the
    goods-conquering, kine-conquering, booty-conquering one, of whom the

    existence.

c.

Griffith

Rohita, conqueror of cows and riches and gathered spoil, is heaven’s and earth’s upholder. Over earth’s greatness would I tell my kinship with thee who hast a thousand births and seven.

рейрео рдпрд╢рд╛ рдпрд╛рд╕рд┐ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Glorious thou goest to the directions and quarters, glorious of
    cattle and of people (carс╣гaс╣З├н); glorious in the lap of earth, of
    Aditi, may I become pleasant (c─Б╠Бru) like Savitar.
Notes

Ppp. reads nu instead of ca in a, and asmi instead of
bh┼лy─Бsam in d; and it combines pс╣Ыthivy─Б тАЩdi- in c. There is
a deficiency of a syllable, unnoticed in the Anukr., in a, unless we
resolve ya-─Бsi.

Griffith

A glorious sight to beasts and men, thou goest glorious to the regions and mid-regions. On earth’s, on Aditi’s bosom, bright with glory. Fain would I equal Savitar in beauty.

  1. Being yonder, thou knowest here; being on this side, thou seest

рекрез рдЕрд╡рдГ рдкрд░реЗрдг ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Below the distant, thus beyond the lower, bearing her calf with her
    foot, the cow hath stood up; whitherwards, to what quarter, hath she
    forsooth gone away? where giveth she birth? for [it is] not in this
    herd.
Notes

This is a repetition of ix. 9. 17, and, as there are two successive
verses beginning with av├бс╕е p├бreс╣Зa, this one is quoted here in the mss.
with the unusual expression av├бh p├бreс╣З├й тАЩd p┼л╠Бrv─Б. тМКThe Anukr.
doubtless balances the extra syllable in a by counting k├║a as one
syllable in d.тМЛ

Griffith

Beneath the upper realm, above this lower, bearing her Calf at foot, the Cow hath risen Whitherward, to what place hath she departed? Where doth she calve? Not in this herd of cattle.

рекреи рдПрдХрдкрджреА рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрджреА ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. One-footed, two-footed [is] she, four-footed; having become
    eight-footed, nine-footed, thousand-syllabled, a series of existence;
    out from her flow apart the oceans.
Notes

This verse is the p─Бdas b-e of ix. 10. 21 (RV. i. 164. 41 b-d,
42 a) тМКsee under ix. 10. 21 for variantsтМЛ. It and the preceding are
very little in place in our hymn. тМКWith d cf. 3. 2 b, below.тМЛ

Griffith

She hath become one-footed or two-footed, four-footed, or eight-footed or nine-footed, This universe’s thousand-syllabled Pankti Oceans flow forth from her in all directions.

Translation
  1. Mounting the sky, immortal, do thou favor my words; sacrifices
    purified by br├бhman carry thee up; yellow roadsters draw thee.
Notes

P─Бdas b and c are identical with 36 a, b. Instead of
adhvagatas, Ppp. reads ghс╣Ыtaс╣Б pibantaс╣Б. Bp. accents pr├б: ├бva.

Griffith

Rising to heaven, immortal, hear my calling. Cleansed by prayer, sacrifices bear thee upward. Bay coursers, ever on the road, convey thee.

Translation
  1. The fire of the sky-finding ruddy one is kindled with br├бhman;
    therefrom heat, therefrom cold, therefrom the sacrifice was born.
Notes

The majority of mss. read correctly yaj├▒├▓ тАЩj─Бy- at the end; the rest
vary between -├▒├│ aj- and -├▒├▓ aj-. Ppp. reads -├▒o aj-; and, in
b, sam─Бhitah for sam idhyate.

Griffith

Rohita’s Agni-his who found heaven’s light-is kindled with the prayer. From him the heat, from him the cold, from him the sacrifice was born.

Both Agins-Rohita’s who found the light of heaven–made strong by prayer, Waxing by prayer, adored with prayer, by prayer enkindled, sacrificed.

Translation
  1. The one is all set in truth, the other is kindled in the waters:
    kindled with etc. etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Having shaped (kс╕╖p) the earth as sacrificial hearth, having made
    the sky sacrificial fee, then having made heat his fire, the ruddy one
    made all that has soul, with rain as sacrificial butter.
Notes
Griffith

Rohita made the earth to be his altar, heaven his Dakshina. Then heat he took for Agni, and with rain for molten butter he created every living thing.

Whitney
Translation
  1. That first sacrifice was born [as] the one that is, that is to be;
    from that was born this all, whatsoever shines out (vi-ruc) here,
    brought (─Б-bhс╣Ы) by the ruddy one [as] seer.
Notes

Ppp. ends the hymn with this verse, although vs. 58 is found in another
place. It combines jaj├▒e тАЩdaс╣Б, as we are doubtless to read, though not
with the sanction of the Anukr., which calls the p─Бda bс╣Ыhat─л. тМКCf. iv.
23. 7.тМЛ

Griffith

This sacrifice, the first of all, the past, the present, had its birth. From that arose this universe, yea, all this world of brightness, brought by Rohita the heavenly Sage.

Translation
  1. Whoever both kicks a cow with the foot and urinates in face of the
    sunтАФof such a one I hew off (vra┼Ыc) thy root; thou shalt not further
    cast (kс╣Ы) shadow.

тМКCf. the note on the vs. concerning posture in urination at vii. 102:
and add that Buddhaghosa, in his comment on the description of the
Acelakas, at D─лgha Nik─Бya, viii. 14 (as reported by Davids, Translation,
p. 227), speaks of the standing posture as wrong.тАФAs to making water
with face towards the sun, cf. MBh. xiii. 104. 75 (5029), and note to
Manu iv. 48 in my Reader, p. 349, and the references there given,
especially the reference to Jolly’s Viс╣гс╣Зu, SBE. vii. 194 f.тАФAs for the
loss of the shadow, cf. the Peter Schlemihl story; also J─Бtaka, i. 102тБ╣;
vi. 337┬╣┬╣.тМЛ

The character of this and the following verses shows that Ppp. has
reason for not making them a part of the hymn. This verse makes its

1.тМЛ

Griffith

If thou should kick a cow, or by indecent act offend the Sun, Thy root I sever; nevermore mayst thou cast shadow on the ground.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou that goest past me shading me, and between me and the fire, I
    hew off thy root; thou shalt not further cast shadow.
Notes

The connection appears to demand this pregnant rendering of abhich─Бy├бm
‘so as to cast thy shadow on’ (so also Ludwig). It is easy to read b
as a regular anuс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda, though the Anukr. allows it only six
syllables.

Griffith

Thou who, between the fire and me, passest across the line of shade. Thy root I sever: nevermore mayst thou cast shadow on the ground.

релреп рдорд╛ рдкреНрд░ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Let us not go forth from the road, nor, O Indra, from the sacrifice
    with soma; let not the niggards stand between us.
Notes

That is, between us and something else, so as to cut us off from our
desire or object. The verse is, without variant, RV. x. 57. 1, and found
also in JB. iii. 168. It is used once in V─Бit. (18. 8), and several
times in K─Бu┼Ы. (54. 18; 82. 6; 89. 11; also by the schol. under 42. 15;
58. 17).

Griffith

Let us not, Indra, leave the path, the Soma-presser’s sacrifice. Let not malignities dwell with us.

Whitney
Translation
  1. What line, accomplisher of the sacrifice, is stretched clear to the
    gods, that, sacrificed unto, may we attain.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 57. 2, which reads at the end na┼Ы─лmahi. It is used
by the schol. to K─Бu┼Ы. 58. 17, with vs. 59, in the ceremony of
name-giving.

тМКHere ends the first anuv─Бka, 1 hymn and 60 verses. The quoted Anukr.
says с╣гaс╣гс╣нiс╕е.тМЛ

Griffith

May we obtain, completely wrought, the thread spun out tc reach the Gods, That perfecteth our sacrifice.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдГ) рдЬреЛ [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп) рдпрдЬреНрдЮ [рджреЗрд╡рдкреВрдЬрд╛, рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рдХрд░рдг, рджрд╛рдирд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░] рдХрд╛ (рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рдзрдирдГ) рдмрдбрд╝рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдзрдХ (рддрдиреНрддреБрдГ) рддрдиреНрддреБ [рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рд░реВрдк] рд╣реЛрдХрд░ (рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ) рджреЗрд╡реЛрдВ [рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ, рд▓реЛрдХреЛрдВ, рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ] рдореЗрдВ (рдЖрддрддрдГ) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдлреИрд▓рд╛ рд╣реИред (рддрдореН рдЖрд╣реБрддрдореН) рдЙрд╕ рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдг рдХрд┐рдпреЗ рдЧрдпреЗ [рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░] рдХреЛ (рдЕрд╢реАрдорд╣рд┐) рд╣рдо рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ рееремрежрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЙрд╕ рдЬрдЧрддреНрдкрд┐рддрд╛, рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдирд┐рдпрдиреНрддрд╛, рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЛ рдзреНрдпрд╛рди рдореЗрдВ рд░рдЦрдХрд░ рдЕрдкрдиреА рдЙрдиреНрдирддрд┐ рдХрд░реЗрдВ рееремрежреердпрд╣ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдХреБрдЫ рднреЗрдж рд╕реЗ рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрдж рдореЗрдВ рд╣реИ-рдореж резрежредрелренредреи рее рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рдердореЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрдГ рее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: ремрежтИТ(рдпрдГ) рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп) рджреЗрд╡рдкреВрдЬрд╛рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рдХрд░рдгрджрд╛рдирд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп (рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рдзрдирдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг рд╕рд╛рдзрдХрдГ (рддрдиреНрддреБрдГ) рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдпрдерд╛ (рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ) рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпреЗрд╖реБ рд▓реЛрдХреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рдЪ (рдЖрддрддрдГ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддреГрддрдГ (рддрдореН) рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдЖрд╣реБрддрдореН) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рджреН рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрдореН (рдЕрд╢реАрдорд╣рд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдпрд╛рдо рее
